ASSAY_COMP_NAME	Acutely hazardous substances
ASSAY_COMP_DESC	Substances in list which are acutely hazardous
ASSAY_COMP_VALUE_TYPE	TEXT
ASSAY_COMP_UNIT
ASSAY_NOTE	Substances notes "A" are acutely hazardous substances
ASSAY_NOTE	"Acutely Hazardous Substance" means a hazardous substance which: (A) has an oral LD50 (rat) toxicity of less than 50 milligrams per kilogram; (B) has an inhalation LC50 (rat) toxicity of less than 2 milligrams per liter; (C) has a dermal LD50 (rabbit) toxicity of less than 200 milligrams per kilogram; or (D) causes or is capable of causing death, serious illness or serious physical injury to any person or persons as a consequence of release into the environment.

ASSAY_NOTE	Current through 4/15/2021
ASSAY_NOTE	Notification of the release of an RQ (Reportable Quantity) of solid particles of antimony, arsenic, beryllium, cadmium, chromium, copper, lead, nickel, selenium, silver, thallium or zinc is not required if the mean diameter of the particles released is larger than 100 micrometers (0.004 inches).
ASSAY_NOTE	The RQ for asbestos is limited to friable forms only.
ASSAY_NOTE	Includes mineral fiber emissions from facilities manufacturing or processing glass, rock, or slag fibers (or other mineral derived fibers) of average diameter one micrometer or less.
ASSAY_NOTE	Includes mono- and di-ethers of ethylene glycol, diethylene glycol, and triethylene glycol R-(OCH2CH2)n-OR’ where: n=1, 2, or 3; R = alkyl C7 or less; or R = phenyl or alkyl substituted phenyl; R’ = H or alkyl C7 or less; or OR’ consisting of carboxylic acid ester, sulfate, phosphate, nitrate, or sulfonate.
ASSAY_NOTE	Includes organic compounds with more than one benzene ring, and which have a boiling point greater than or equal to 100°C.
ASSAY_NOTE	OFFICIAL COMPILATION OF CODES, RULES AND REGULATIONS OF THE STATE OF NEW YORK/TITLE 6. DEPARTMENT OF ENVIRONMENTAL CONSERVATION/CHAPTER V. RESOURCE MANAGEMENT SERVICES/SUBCHAPTER E. WATER REGULATION PART 597. HAZARDOUS SUBSTANCES IDENTIFICATION, RELEASE PROHIBITION, AND RELEASE REPORTING

ASSAY_NOTE	Between 1997 and 2003, the New York State Department of Health (NYSDOH) conducted a study of the occurrence of volatile organic chemicals (VOCs) in the indoor air of homes that heat with fuel oil.
ASSAY_NOTE	The study included basement, living space and outdoor samples from 104 homes, tested during both heating and non-heating seasons.
ASSAY_NOTE	With the exception of New York City, homes from across the state were included in the study, with the majority of the homes being near the Albany area.

ASSAY_COMP_DESC	Classification of Surface and Ground Waters. See regulation for complete description of classification
ASSAY_COMP_VALUE_TYPE	TEXT
ASSAY_COMP_UNIT
ASSAY_NOTE	�701.2 Class N fresh surface waters. Uses are as a source of water for drinking or culinary purposes, bathing, fishing, fish propagation, and recreation. The waters shall be suitable for shellfish and wildlife propagation and survival and fish survival.
ASSAY_NOTE	�701.3 Class AA-Special (AA-S) fresh surface waters. Uses are water supply for drinking, culinary or food processing purposes; primary and secondary contact recreation; and fishing. The waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival.
ASSAY_NOTE	�701.4 Class A-Special (A-S) fresh surface waters. Uses are as a source of water supply for drinking, culinary or food processing purposes; primary and secondary contact recreation; and fishing. The waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival.
ASSAY_NOTE	�701.6 Class A fresh surface waters. Uses are as a source of water supply for drinking, culinary or food processing purposes; primary and secondary contact recreation; and fishing. The waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival.
ASSAY_NOTE	�701.7 Class B fresh surface waters. The best usages of Class B waters are primary and secondary contact recreation and fishing. These waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival.
ASSAY_NOTE	�701.8 Class C fresh surface waters. The best usage of Class C waters is fishing. These waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival. The water quality shall be suitable for primary and secondary contact recreation, although other factors may limit the use for these purposes.
ASSAY_NOTE	�701.9 Class D fresh surface waters. The best usage of Class D waters is fishing. Due to such natural conditions as intermittency of flow, water conditions not conducive to propagation of game fishery, or stream bed conditions, the waters will not support fish propagation. These waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife survival. The water quality shall be suitable for primary and secondary contact recreation, although other factors may limit the use for these purposes.
ASSAY_NOTE	�701.10 Class SA saline surface waters. The best usages of Class SA waters are shellfishing for market purposes, primary and secondary contact recreation and fishing. These waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival.
ASSAY_NOTE	�701.11 Class SB saline surface waters. The best usages of Class SB waters are primary and secondary contact recreation and fishing. These waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival.
ASSAY_NOTE	�701.12 Class SC saline surface waters. The best usage of Class SC waters is fishing. These waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival. The water quality shall be suitable for primary and secondary contact recreation, although other factors may limit the use for these purposes.
ASSAY_NOTE	�701.13 Class I saline surface waters. The best usages of Class I waters are secondary contact recreation and fishing. These waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival.
ASSAY_NOTE	�701.14 Class SD saline surface waters. The best usage of Class SD waters is fishing. These waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife survival. This classification may be given to those waters that, because of natural or man-made conditions, cannot meet the requirements for primary and secondary contact recreation and fish propagation.
ASSAY_NOTE	�701.15 Class GA fresh groundwaters. The best usage of Class GA waters is as a source of potable water supply. Class GA waters are fresh groundwaters.
ASSAY_NOTE	�701.16 Class GSA saline groundwaters. The best usages of Class GSA waters are as a source of potable mineral waters, or conversion to fresh potable waters, or as raw material for the manufacture of sodium chloride or its derivatives or similar products. Class GSA waters are saline groundwaters.
ASSAY_NOTE	�701.17 Class GSB saline groundwaters. The best usage of Class GSB waters is as a receiving water for disposal of wastes. Class GSB waters are saline groundwaters that have a chloride concentration in excess of 1,000 milligrams per liter or a total dissolved solids concentration in excess of 2,000 milligrams per liter.

SOURCE_NAME_AID	NY_Pesticide_EIQ_AID_1
DATA_COLLECTION	NY Pesticide EIQ
ASSAY_NAME	New York State calculation of environmental impact quotient, EIQ, of pesticides
ASSAY_DESCRIPTION	New York State method of calculation of environmental impact quotient, EIQ for pesticides used on fruit and vegetables
ASSAY_CATEGORY	Media concentration-water
ASSAY_CATEGORY	Regulation
ASSAY_URL	http://ecommons.cornell.edu/bitstream/1813/5203/1/FLS-139.pdf
ASSAY_NOTE	New York's Food and Life Sciences Bulletin: A Method To Measure The Environmental Impact Of Pesticides; J. Kovach, C. Petzoldt, J. Degnil, and J. Tette; Number 139, 1992
ASSAY_NOTE	Method to calculate the environmental impact (environmental impact quotient, EIQ) of most common fruit and vegetable pesticides (insecticides, acaricides, fungicides and herbicides) used in commercial agriculture
ASSAY_NOTE	published environmental impact information of pesticides was used in the model
ASSAY_NOTE	an equation was developed based on the three principal components of agricultural production systems: a farm worker component, a consumer component, and an ecological component. Each component in the equation is given equal weight in the final analysis, but within each component, individual factors are weighted differently.

DATA_COLLECTION	NY DEC Water QS GV 1998
ASSAY_NAME	New York DEC Water Quality Standards and Guidance Values (1998)
ASSAY_DESCRIPTION	New York State Department of Environmental Conservation (DEC) Ambient water Quality Standards and Guidance Values (June 1998)
ASSAY_URL	https://www.dec.ny.gov/chemical/23853.html
ASSAY_NOTE	Water quality standards and standard-setting procedures are in 6 NYCRR Chapter X, Parts 700-706.
ASSAY_NOTE	Document: TOGS 1.1.3 (PDF) - Procedures for derivation site-specific standards and guidance values for protection of aquatic life
ASSAY_NOTE	Reissued Date: JUNE 1998. There are subsequent amendments
ASSAY_NOTE	Data from  table 1 NEW YORK STATE AMBIENT WATER QUALITY STANDARDS AND GUIDANCE VALUES JUNE 1998
ASSAY_NOTE	Class N fresh surface waters. Uses are as a source of water for drinking or culinary purposes, bathing, fishing, fish propagation, and recreation. The waters shall be suitable for shellfish and wildlife propagation and survival and fish survival.
ASSAY_NOTE	Class AA-Special (AA-S) fresh surface waters. Uses are water supply for drinking, culinary or food processing purposes; primary and secondary contact recreation; and fishing. The waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival.
ASSAY_NOTE	Class A-Special (A-S) fresh surface waters. Uses are as a source of water supply for drinking, culinary or food processing purposes; primary and secondary contact recreation; and fishing. The waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival.
ASSAY_NOTE	Class A fresh surface waters. Uses are as a source of water supply for drinking, culinary or food processing purposes; primary and secondary contact recreation; and fishing. The waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival.
ASSAY_NOTE	Class B fresh surface waters. The best usages of Class B waters are primary and secondary contact recreation and fishing. These waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival.
ASSAY_NOTE	Class C fresh surface waters. The best usage of Class C waters is fishing. These waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival. The water quality shall be suitable for primary and secondary contact recreation, although other factors may limit the use for these purposes.
ASSAY_NOTE	Class D fresh surface waters. The best usage of Class D waters is fishing. Due to such natural conditions as intermittency of flow, water conditions not conducive to propagation of game fishery, or stream bed conditions, the waters will not support fish propagation. These waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife survival. The water quality shall be suitable for primary and secondary contact recreation, although other factors may limit the use for these purposes.
ASSAY_NOTE	Class SA saline surface waters. The best usages of Class SA waters are shellfishing for market purposes, primary and secondary contact recreation and fishing. These waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival.
ASSAY_NOTE	Class SB saline surface waters. The best usages of Class SB waters are primary and secondary contact recreation and fishing. These waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival.
ASSAY_NOTE	Class SC saline surface waters. The best usage of Class SC waters is fishing. These waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival. The water quality shall be suitable for primary and secondary contact recreation, although other factors may limit the use for these purposes.
ASSAY_NOTE	Class I saline surface waters. The best usages of Class I waters are secondary contact recreation and fishing. These waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife propagation and survival.
ASSAY_NOTE	Class SD saline surface waters. The best usage of Class SD waters is fishing. These waters shall be suitable for fish, shellfish, and wildlife survival. This classification may be given to those waters that, because of natural or man-made conditions, cannot meet the requirements for primary and secondary contact recreation and fish propagation.
ASSAY_NOTE	Class GA fresh groundwaters. The best usage of Class GA waters is as a source of potable water supply. Class GA waters are fresh groundwaters.
ASSAY_NOTE	Class GSA saline groundwaters. The best usages of Class GSA waters are as a source of potable mineral waters, or conversion to fresh potable waters, or as raw material for the manufacture of sodium chloride or its derivatives or similar products. Class GSA waters are saline groundwaters.
ASSAY_NOTE	Class GSB saline groundwaters. The best usage of Class GSB waters is as a receiving water for disposal of wastes. Class GSB waters are saline groundwaters that have a chloride concentration in excess of 1,000 milligrams per liter or a total dissolved solids concentration in excess of 2,000 milligrams per liter.

ASSAY_NOTE	There are 89 permanent groundwater monitoring wells;  total of 95 temporary or permanent groundwater monitoring wells
ASSAY_NOTE	The McCaffrey Street facility was built in 1961, and had been used to manufacture circuit board laminates, polytetrafluoroethylene (PTFE)-coated fiberglass and other PTFE products. In 1999 it began using PFOA in its manufacturing.

ASSAY_NOTE	Hoosick Falls Area Information for Communities Impacted by Per- and Poly-fluorinated Aklyl Substances (PFAS): Validated PFAS Results for Village Water System (PDF), January 2018
ASSAY_NOTE	Work to date has included collection of samples from soil, groundwater and surface water.
ASSAY_NOTE	Environmental Testing and Cleanup McCaffrey Street and Liberty streets (Saint-Gobain Performance Plastics Sites, SGPP)
ASSAY_NOTE	The McCaffrey Street facility was built in 1961, and had been used to manufacture circuit board laminates, polytetrafluoroethylene (PTFE)-coated fiberglass and other PTFE products. In 1999 it began using PFOA in its manufacturing.
